<div id="descriptionContainer">
      <div style="right:0" class="readable stacked" id="description">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer7448076727548520118">Twelve-year-old Addie admires her older sister Meryl, who aspires to rid the kingdom of Bamarre of gryphons, specters, and ogres. Addie, on the other hand, is fearful even of spiders and depends on Meryl for courage and protection. Waving her sword Bloodbiter, the older girl declaims in the garden from the heroic epic of Drualt to a thrilled audience of Addie, their govern</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7448076727548520118">Twelve-year-old Addie admires her older sister Meryl, who aspires to rid the kingdom of Bamarre of gryphons, specters, and ogres. Addie, on the other hand, is fearful even of spiders and depends on Meryl for courage and protection. Waving her sword Bloodbiter, the older girl declaims in the garden from the heroic epic of Drualt to a thrilled audience of Addie, their governess, and the young sorcerer Rhys. <br /><br />But when Meryl falls ill with the dreaded Gray Death, Addie must gather her courage and set off alone on a quest to find the cure and save her beloved sister. Addie takes the seven-league boots and magic spyglass left to her by her mother and the enchanted tablecloth and cloak given to her by Rhys - along with a shy declaration of his love. She prevails in encounters with tricky specters (spiders too) and outwits a wickedly personable dragon in adventures touched with romance and a bittersweet ending.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7448076727548520118">...more</a>

        rated it

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">girls who are into those wimpy Disney princesses and anyone who wants to read a good adventure</span></div>

        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/142816-heavyreader?shelf=young-adult" class="actionLinkLite">young-adult</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer41359574">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3530605176694224503">This book is so good!<br /><br />It did take me a while to get into it. The first half or so of the book is kind of slow going. Two sisters. One is bold. One is shy. Yawn.<br /><br />But then in the middle, when the shy sister has to leave the castle to save her beloved sister's life, it gets REALLY exciting. Specters. Gryphons. Dragons. Battles. WOW! I could hardly put it down at that point.<br /><br />There's also a story within a story, a legend of the kingdom, and it is as well done as the main story.<br /><br />The almost end had me bawl</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3530605176694224503">This book is so good!<br /><br />It did take me a while to get into it. The first half or so of the book is kind of slow going. Two sisters. One is bold. One is shy. Yawn.<br /><br />But then in the middle, when the shy sister has to leave the castle to save her beloved sister's life, it gets REALLY exciting. Specters. Gryphons. Dragons. Battles. WOW! I could hardly put it down at that point.<br /><br />There's also a story within a story, a legend of the kingdom, and it is as well done as the main story.<br /><br />The almost end had me bawling, thinking about my own sister and how terrible it would be to lose her.<br /><br />I don't typically get into stories about princesses. As Boots of the Coup says, "Tell your teacher I said princess <em>are</em> evil/How they got all their money was to kill people." But I can stomach the feisty, smart, brave princesses in the books of Gail Carson Levine. She spins the whole traditional princess genre and makes these gals rock!<br /><br />Unlike other books by Gail Carson Levine, this one is not based on a traditional fairy tale (or at least not one that I know), but it's better than any of those "someday my prince will come" bullshit stories that I grew up with.<br /><br />Give this one to the girl in your life who's all into those wimpy Disney princesses.</span>

It's one I loved from beginning to end, and it's one that I never tire of reading over and over again. It's the only book I've read more times than I can count on my one hand and several more on the other. This is an awesome read with great morals about finding courage in a world that is against you doing so. It's about family and the beauty of being there for each other, even if you're not quiet the same. It's got poetry, dragons, action, suspense, all the good stuff...and it's in one read. <div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_447318189">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/447318189" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/12678407-naomi-brist" class="left imgcol" title="Naomi Brist"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1347211693p2/12678407.jpg" alt="Naomi Brist" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/447318189?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 13, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/12678407-naomi-brist" class="user" title="Naomi Brist">Naomi Brist</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/12678407-naomi-brist?shelf=favorites" class="actionLinkLite">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer447318189">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3656869165011100005">I've grown up with this story. To say that it has had an impact on my life is an incredible and unforgivable understatement. Everyone knows this author because of Ella Enchanted, but I believe that this book is much, much greater. It has romance, monsters, action, magic, and adventure; all things that people look for and enjoy in a good book. But what really makes this story great is not any of those things. What makes it great is how a young woman who is afraid of everything ventures out into a</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3656869165011100005">I've grown up with this story. To say that it has had an impact on my life is an incredible and unforgivable understatement. Everyone knows this author because of Ella Enchanted, but I believe that this book is much, much greater. It has romance, monsters, action, magic, and adventure; all things that people look for and enjoy in a good book. But what really makes this story great is not any of those things. What makes it great is how a young woman who is afraid of everything ventures out into a dangerous and terrifying world that would scare even the brave in order to save her sister even though there is a very high chance she might die in the attempt. Speaking as someone who has a lot of experience being afraid, this story is inspiring and very relatable in so many important areas. Because even those of us who are afraid of a great many things would go to frightening lengths and do the impossible to save someone we love. <br /><br />Two Princesses of Bamarre is a fantastic fairy tale that contains all the best elements of such stories and has more heart than stories written by authors that are supposed to be 'good'. If the apocalypse came tomorrow and there was only one book that I could keep with me and read again it would be this one. I love many books, but this is a part of my soul and is beyond beautiful. If you like fantasy and are not opposed to actual emotion (if you are then you are next on my hit list) then you should read this book. It is the fairy tale that surpasses all fairy tales and puts the Grimm brothers to shame. Thank you, Gail Carson Levine, for writing such an amazing story. You're one of the greatest reasons I myself plan on becoming a writer. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3656869165011100005">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_44097181">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/44097181" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1947586-megan" class="left imgcol" title="Megan"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1363746570p2/1947586.jpg" alt="Megan" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/44097181?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 31, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1947586-megan" class="user" title="Megan">Megan</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/820241.The_Two_Princesses_of_Bamarre" title="Hardcover 9780060293154" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1947586-megan?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer44097181">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14794631661346207233">This book was really cute! It's written in the first person, which was a change, as few of the books I read are, and the protagonist of the story is Princess Addie, a sweet but cowardly girl who couldn't be more different than her sister, Meryl. Princess Meryl is courageous and longs for adventures where she can kill dragons, gryphons, and ogres. Addie would rather stay safe at home and wishes for peace, not wars like her sister. The two are even opposites in appearance. Addie has dark brown hai</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14794631661346207233">This book was really cute! It's written in the first person, which was a change, as few of the books I read are, and the protagonist of the story is Princess Addie, a sweet but cowardly girl who couldn't be more different than her sister, Meryl. Princess Meryl is courageous and longs for adventures where she can kill dragons, gryphons, and ogres. Addie would rather stay safe at home and wishes for peace, not wars like her sister. The two are even opposites in appearance. Addie has dark brown hair and is tall while Meryl has blonde hair and is short.<br /><br />Still they are very close, and when Meryl contracts the Gray Death, of which there is no cure, Addie decides to overcome her fears and sets out to find a cure. Along the way she finds help from her father's sorcerer, Rhys, with whom she falls in love. The background of sorcerers in this story was very interesting. They're born when lightning strikes marble, and therefore have no family, and instead of a heartbeat, they have a life flame burning in their chests. Sorcerers can be male or female, but all have dark wavy hair and white eyelashes. Their magic usually consists of manipulating clouds into different shapes for different purposes, and perhaps the most amazing thing of all is that they can fly.<br /><br />On Addie's adventure, she comes up against ogres, gryphons, and a dragon, all while trying to find a cure for her sister, who doesn't have much time left. The ending was surprising and not what I expected exactly, but I really enjoyed this book. It's geared towards young adults and was only a little over 200 pages.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14794631661346207233">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/645771513?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 11, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/13635411-gabs" class="user" title="Gabs">Gabs</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/13635411-gabs?shelf=2013-favorites" class="actionLinkLite">2013-favorites</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/13635411-gabs?shelf=possible-automatic-buy-authors" class="actionLinkLite">possible-automatic-buy-authors</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer645771513">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6879038326185784398">I didn't think that Gail Carson Levine could write anything more spectacular than Ella Enchanted. I'm not going to say that The Two Princesses of Bamarre was better than Ella Enchanted, but it definitely was as good as it. <br /><br />Addie and Meryl had such a great relationship. I loved reading about them, and how Addie was willing to risk her life to save her sister from the Gray Death. <br /><br />Rhys...sigh. Oh, Rhys. He's a very attractive sorceror, and I loved him! Gail Carson Levine created a romance that wasn</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6879038326185784398">I didn't think that Gail Carson Levine could write anything more spectacular than Ella Enchanted. I'm not going to say that The Two Princesses of Bamarre was better than Ella Enchanted, but it definitely was as good as it. <br /><br />Addie and Meryl had such a great relationship. I loved reading about them, and how Addie was willing to risk her life to save her sister from the Gray Death. <br /><br />Rhys...sigh. Oh, Rhys. He's a very attractive sorceror, and I loved him! Gail Carson Levine created a romance that wasn't cheesy or over the top romantic, but was very sweet and great to read.<br /><br />It was refreshing to read a fairy tale that hadn't been written before, because I had no idea how it would end! I was very impressed with the ending, as well. It was unexpected, but satisfying.<br /><br />The monsters in here are also pretty fun to learn about. THe specters, the gryphons, the ogres, and the dragons were all portrayed in a new way, and some I hadn't even read of before! <br /><br />All together, I gave this five stars because it is an amazing, original tale that kept my interest. It has a good chance of becoming one of my all-time favorites!</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6879038326185784398">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <a href="/user/show/19752859-sydney-cornwall" class="user" title="Sydney Cornwall">Sydney Cornwall</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/19752859-sydney-cornwall?shelf=eng-356" class="actionLinkLite">eng-356</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a onclick="Effect.toggle('reviewTextContainer615383554'); return false;" href="#">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span style="display:none" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer615383554">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4913885621738058230">Plot Summary:<br /><br />The plot revolves around two sisters, Meryl and Addie. They are the princesses of Bamarre, a fantastical kingdom where sorcerers, fairies, and dragons are commonly known to be in existence. Addie is the shy, timid younger sister stereotype; she spends her free time doing embroidery. Meryl, on the other hand, loves adventure and swords and fighting. Addie makes Meryl promise her that she won't go off to kill any dragons or anything until Addie gets married--but everything gets thrown</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4913885621738058230">Plot Summary:<br /><br />The plot revolves around two sisters, Meryl and Addie. They are the princesses of Bamarre, a fantastical kingdom where sorcerers, fairies, and dragons are commonly known to be in existence. Addie is the shy, timid younger sister stereotype; she spends her free time doing embroidery. Meryl, on the other hand, loves adventure and swords and fighting. Addie makes Meryl promise her that she won't go off to kill any dragons or anything until Addie gets married--but everything gets thrown into a frenzy when Meryl catches the Grey Death. Addie has to step up and try to find the cure when her father turns into a pansy and doesn't try very hard. She encounters griffons, specters, and dragons; she has to learn to be confident and believe in herself. In the end, she does find the cure to the Grey Death. She's too late to save her sister; however, and Meryl encounters the transformation into a fairy, a very sacred being. Addie kind of brings the kingdom out of the terror from dark creatures and the Grey Death, a curse brought upon by a dragon of late, becomes diminished.<br /><br />My Opinion:<br />I rated this book a two. I didn't really enjoy reading it. I have to say, for a younger reader, it's a good choice--there are great lessons to be learned; also (though it's done very blatantly) the protagonist shows a lot of character development throughout the course of the book. There's a nice unpredictable twist at the end--I very much expected Meryl to be saved from the Grey Death and was surprised with the ingenuity of the final result. I think it's a good story, but I'm just very cynical and felt like it was too simply and immaturely written for me, but that's just me. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4913885621738058230">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_1406855955">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1406855955" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/45951450-samantha" class="left imgcol" title="Samantha"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1452046228p2/45951450.jpg" alt="Samantha" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1406855955?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 18, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/45951450-samantha" class="user" title="Samantha">Samantha</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/45951450-samantha?shelf=didn-t-like-the-ending" class="actionLinkLite">didn-t-like-the-ending</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/45951450-samantha?shelf=annoying-heroine" class="actionLinkLite">annoying-heroine</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/45951450-samantha?shelf=could-use-some-work" class="actionLinkLite">could-use-some-work</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1406855955">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2514363357381670484">I really didn't like this one. The book makes it a point that Princess Addie is the shy mousy one, while Princess Meryl is the adventurous hero type. To be honest, I think it would of been better if Addie had been the one sick, and the book focused on Meryl's first experience with a real life adventure, not just dreaming of goin on one. It might of been more believable that way. This is a sort of rant.<br /><br /><strong> SPOILERS </strong><br /><strong> The Beginning: </strong> Seriously? Princess Addie, the girl who's so afraid of spiders, mana</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2514363357381670484">I really didn't like this one. The book makes it a point that Princess Addie is the shy mousy one, while Princess Meryl is the adventurous hero type. To be honest, I think it would of been better if Addie had been the one sick, and the book focused on Meryl's first experience with a real life adventure, not just dreaming of goin on one. It might of been more believable that way. This is a sort of rant.<br /><br /><strong> SPOILERS </strong><br /><strong> The Beginning: </strong> Seriously? Princess Addie, the girl who's so afraid of spiders, manages to do some quick thinking, and kills an ogre, her brain clouded by mortal fear? Yes I get she has the preservation of her sisters life to keep her goin, but with no former background or experience, she kills an ogre, on the first day of her adventure.<br /><strong> The middle: </strong> really. She takes a step in the boots, get up close and personal with the dragon Vollys, who's volatile and scares the living daylights out of Addie, and stabs her with a sword that she knows nothin of how to use? Also, quick question, Vollys mother, Yune, got stabbed by a human and died that way, Vollys knows this, she's a old dragon, and has managed to live longer than 700 years at least, yet, she opens the boulder to her cave, which houses a number of weapons, and a human in it, without fully knowing what Addie was doing? She obviously knew Addie was up to something <em> "I know you're wearing those boots of yours" </em> yes I know she flamed it first, but why take the risk? She left her self open to attack behind the flames, dragons have years of experience and wisdom, yet she thought she would be safe behind some fire (how did the fire stay there when she moved the boulder, by the way? <em> she pushed the boulder aside and left behind a wall of flames </em> the way I understand that, Vollys pushed away the boulder, leaving its fire magically floating in the air. ?!?!?!<br /><strong> the end: </strong> this is going to be a long one, there was so many questions I had. First off, after being in the real world alone with virtually no help for the first time in your life, and only for a week or so, that does not magically turn you into a gryphon and ogre slaying heroine that magically knows a little swordplay, with no real former training. Also, how in the world does she throw a sword that's hits home on Vollys' neck? A moving dragons slender neck, to be specific. That just doesn't happen. Either she found the worlds biggest four leaf clover or Vollys death wasn't thought out well. Don't even get me started on Meryl's fate. Seriously? A fairy? Meryl technically is no longer Meryl, by the way, the Gray Death killed her, and what's left is fairy with Meryl's face, as Addie mentioned several times. And what about this little romance with Drualt? She's been a fairy for not even a week, and already has the hero of Bamarre smitten. By the way, when Addie's mother and father die, who's going to rule? Meryl already said she is staying with the fairies, because Addie no longer needs her, but what about the whole kingdom of Bamarre? Meryl is the firstborn, traditionally, the eldest always takes the throne. The next option would be Addie, but, as her new husband is Rhys the sorcerer, how would that even work? Lemme clarify, the kingdom will be all peachy when Addie reigns, but what with when she dies? Naturally, you'd Rhys would rule as King, as a sorcerer he lives much longer than humans, but, sorcerers supposedly lose all interest in human affairs around 200, and Rhys is roughly 80. Addie will be long-dead by the time he's 200, so who would rule? I guess Addie's kids would, but they'd be half sorcerer, how would that affect them? I guess an alternate option would be Meryl and Drualt ruling forever, as they're immortal, but maybe I'm over thinking this. There's just some not well thought out parts, maybe if the author would have expanded on things at certain points in the book, it would be better</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2514363357381670484">...more</a>

          </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer6468421">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7452573729985515986">Cute and funny (like all of Gail Carson Levine's books! :D)!!<br /><br />Gail Carson Levine here creates a fairy tale of her own and gives it a characteristic grrrl-power twist. Twelve-year-old Addie admires her older sister Meryl, who aspires to rid the kingdom of Bamarre of gryphons, specters, and ogres. Addie, on the other hand, is fearful even of spiders and depends on Meryl for courage and protection. Waving her sword Bloodbiter, the older girl declaims in the garden from the heroic epic of Drualt to a</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7452573729985515986">Cute and funny (like all of Gail Carson Levine's books! :D)!!<br /><br />Gail Carson Levine here creates a fairy tale of her own and gives it a characteristic grrrl-power twist. Twelve-year-old Addie admires her older sister Meryl, who aspires to rid the kingdom of Bamarre of gryphons, specters, and ogres. Addie, on the other hand, is fearful even of spiders and depends on Meryl for courage and protection. Waving her sword Bloodbiter, the older girl declaims in the garden from the heroic epic of Drualt to a thrilled audience of Addie, their governess, and the young sorcerer Rhys. But when Meryl falls ill with the dreaded Gray Death, Addie must gather her courage and set off alone on a quest to find the cure and save her beloved sister. Addie takes the seven-league boots and magic spyglass left to her by her mother and the enchanted tablecloth and cloak given to her by Rhys--along with a shy declaration of his love. She prevails in encounters with tricky specters (spiders too) and outwits a wickedly personable dragon in adventures touched with romance and a bittersweet ending. Young fans of princess stories will gobble this one up.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7452573729985515986">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer16624786778194539987">This is a kids' book, so I'm going to excuse the simplistic writing style and clunky plot. It also could have done without the insta-romance, but what I loved about the story was that the protagonist was afraid of everything. I'm tired of heroes who kick ass and do amazing things without batting an eyelash. It's like every hero has to be some kind of adrenaline junkie with a death wish. Addie is a homebody who prefers embroidery to slaying dragons. Yet, when called upon, she doesn't let her fear</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16624786778194539987">This is a kids' book, so I'm going to excuse the simplistic writing style and clunky plot. It also could have done without the insta-romance, but what I loved about the story was that the protagonist was afraid of everything. I'm tired of heroes who kick ass and do amazing things without batting an eyelash. It's like every hero has to be some kind of adrenaline junkie with a death wish. Addie is a homebody who prefers embroidery to slaying dragons. Yet, when called upon, she doesn't let her fears get in the way of doing the right thing. It's quite refreshing.</span>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1213554587752312988">I did exactly what my mother told me not to do last night, stay up late and read a book all the way through. I have been in a reading slump for a while having drowned in children’s books this semester and my adult book well I started it in the summer and am about halfway through. I thought a quick something I’ve really wanted to read would get me back in the groove. Addie is afraid of everything. Her sister Meryl is the brave one who protects her. Then the tables are turned and Addie must take up the dangerous quest her sister has always sworn to do. Addie may be a princess but she reads like your average young woman. I think everyone either is an Addie or a Meryl and whether it is a friend or a sibling you have the other sister in your life too. (I’m an Addie.) I actually think this might be my new favorite Gail Carson Levine. I think it is the most heartfelt though I did feel a little cheesy at the end but we all need some happy ending now and then. This one also has the added bonus of there being no movie version to haunt me.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/7541631-hayley-larson?shelf=my-favorites" class="actionLinkLite">my-favorites</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer299203231">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14299308882961921406">Gail Carson Levine captivated me once again with her tale, "the Two Princesses of Bamarre." This was also one of my favorite books in middle school and I read it more than once. I could really connect with the story because I also have a sister who I would do anything for and even though we are different, we get along and really help each other out. As you may have guessed the story tells about two sisters whose father rules over the kingdom of Bamarre which for some time has been plagued with t</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14299308882961921406">Gail Carson Levine captivated me once again with her tale, "the Two Princesses of Bamarre." This was also one of my favorite books in middle school and I read it more than once. I could really connect with the story because I also have a sister who I would do anything for and even though we are different, we get along and really help each other out. As you may have guessed the story tells about two sisters whose father rules over the kingdom of Bamarre which for some time has been plagued with the gray death. Meryl, the brave sister yearns for adventure and wants to conquer this affliction. However, it is Meryl that falls ill with the gray death and it is up to her meek sister Addie to save her. I liked that the story showed Addie overcoming her fears. Another thing I really enjoyed were the magical objects she had to help her. I thought that they were imaginative and so useful. For example, she had boots that dizzily transported her wherever she needed to go and a tablecloth which, once spread out, provided a bountiful meal. I have always loved the fantasy genre and this book really exemplified fantasy for me at the time. It had magic and mystical creatures, was set in a faraway land and had a story I could really connect with. This book is a great read for middle graders and has a lot of valuable lessons such as bravery, helping your family and perseverance. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14299308882961921406">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer703117462">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5008889588712352925"> At first, I thought that since this book was going to be too princess-y, and medieval time-ish, I asked myself, "Why bother?" <br /><br /><br /> My conscious had told me, "Suck it up and read it fool. You'll like it. You always like princesses, now."<br /><br /><br /> And I did. Like it, I mean. This wonderful, original story has been on of my favorites. I loved it! I don't remember much, but I do remember about the princess thinking she was frail, weak, not strong at all like the older one, going on a bunch of journeys. She had</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5008889588712352925"> At first, I thought that since this book was going to be too princess-y, and medieval time-ish, I asked myself, "Why bother?" <br /><br /><br /> My conscious had told me, "Suck it up and read it fool. You'll like it. You always like princesses, now."<br /><br /><br /> And I did. Like it, I mean. This wonderful, original story has been on of my favorites. I loved it! I don't remember much, but I do remember about the princess thinking she was frail, weak, not strong at all like the older one, going on a bunch of journeys. She had some kind of cloth, I think, and with it, she had to say a few words, and then "_Voila!_" it contained so much food, and it was actually GOOD. That was like my day today, actually. I had a birthday party, (yes, I still love the parties. Nice get together with friends actually, so you don't lose touch, you know?) With brownies, cake, chips, pretzels, and the amazing popcorn. :) It all made me smile.<br /><br /><br /> So, anyways, I also remember this adventurous part with the dragon, and it had held her imprisoned in her cave. I forget how she found a way out. I honestly need to check this book out of the library again. It was a magnificent story, one that I will truly never forget. I suggest this book for everyone, from the elderly, to eight year olds. Are there eight year olds on here? That would be weird. But we can live with it. It doesn't matter, ya know? Although it would be weird. So yeah, if you have not read this book, read it!<br /><br /><br />Audrey</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_276507944">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/276507944" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/276443-jami" class="left imgcol" title="Jami"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1419921831p2/276443.jpg" alt="Jami" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/276507944?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 12, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/276443-jami" class="user" title="Jami">Jami</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Jami by: </span>
      Shandi
  </div>



          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/276443-jami?shelf=young-adult" class="actionLinkLite">young-adult</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/276443-jami?shelf=middle-grades" class="actionLinkLite">middle-grades</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer276507944">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6593587882638902273">I liked this book. It was a fairly fast-paced, fun adventure. Two sisters, the princesses of the kingdom of Bamarre, at first glance appear to be very different. Meryl is brave and desperate for adventure. Addie, on the other hand, is fearful of everything, particularly of losing her sister.<br /><br />What transpires is that Addie must embark on an adventure to save her sister. She discovers her own courage, and in the end works with a small group of brave Bamarrians to save the day. <br /><br />I liked the descriptio</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6593587882638902273">I liked this book. It was a fairly fast-paced, fun adventure. Two sisters, the princesses of the kingdom of Bamarre, at first glance appear to be very different. Meryl is brave and desperate for adventure. Addie, on the other hand, is fearful of everything, particularly of losing her sister.<br /><br />What transpires is that Addie must embark on an adventure to save her sister. She discovers her own courage, and in the end works with a small group of brave Bamarrians to save the day. <br /><br />I liked the descriptions of the monsters of Bamarre: the dragons, gryphons, spectres, and ogres. And Addie herself was good and clever, loyal and kind. She even gets up a bit of romance in the end.<br /><br />Somehow, though, this book was missing something for me. Maybe it just read a little too young. Or maybe it was that, other than her proposed fears (which she quickly overcame), Addie just had no flaws. She didn't seem to have a lot of depth to her character. She was very much a fairy-tale character, as were most of the characters in the book -- all good or all bad. <br /><br />That doesn't make this a bad book. I enjoyed reading it, and I thought it was sweet, but it lacked the character development and strength of Levine's <a title="Ella Enchanted by Gail Carson Levine" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24337.Ella_Enchanted">Ella Enchanted</a>.<br /><br />And one other issue I had trouble figuring out: is Addie really only 12?? The story starts out with her at this age, and no significant time appears to have passed before her adventure begins. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[Both she and her sister act young . . . that is, until the end when suddenly they are both romantically involved and Addie is getting married! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I wasn't sure what to make of that.<!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6593587882638902273">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/177848253" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3323445-trini" class="left imgcol" title="Trini"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1317492448p2/3323445.jpg" alt="Trini" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/177848253?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 18, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3323445-trini" class="user" title="Trini">Trini</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer177848253">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4824117238170332673">I read this book first when I was a little kid, sometime between fourth and fifth grade, I think. It was one of the most influential books of my childhood, so it only made sense that I reread all grown up as I am.<br /><br />It wasn't as stunning as I remember it being when I was a kid, but it was still really amazing. The story-telling and the feeling in the book was something that you don't find in some of the 'finer' books of this time. And maybe it was more because of my nostalgia than because of the po</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4824117238170332673">I read this book first when I was a little kid, sometime between fourth and fifth grade, I think. It was one of the most influential books of my childhood, so it only made sense that I reread all grown up as I am.<br /><br />It wasn't as stunning as I remember it being when I was a kid, but it was still really amazing. The story-telling and the feeling in the book was something that you don't find in some of the 'finer' books of this time. And maybe it was more because of my nostalgia than because of the power of this book, but at the end I teared up a little as I remembered how much I loved it and why I loved it and even though its theme wasn't something mindblowing it was a universal truth and it was something that would always hold true.<br /><br />So maybe it was the power of this book that made me want to cry--this power that lasted over the years since I read it and reminded me of my childhood and made me nostalgic and remember why Gail Carson Levine is my favorite children's author of all time.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4824117238170332673">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9451784913213151878">Ok, the whole book, the whole great book, was RUINED by the horrible ending. <br />First of all, I like that Meryl, the daring, adventurous, passionate one, was small. I love it when the small people are like that. Also, I love that Meryl was the oldest 'cause a lot of people protray the oldest as some wimpy, over-mature person who never gets into any adventures.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText9451784913213151878">Ok, the whole book, the whole great book, was RUINED by the horrible ending. <br />First of all, I like that Meryl, the daring, adventurous, passionate one, was small. I love it when the small people are like that. Also, I love that Meryl was the oldest 'cause a lot of people protray the oldest as some wimpy, over-mature person who never gets into any adventures. Finally, the firstborn is the spitfire! <br />And then I liked the twists, that Addie had to go and conquer all of her fears and learn to be strong and courageous. <br />But then, instead of being cured to fight battles and save her kingdom, fiery Meryl becomes a fairy- a FAIRY, people. But worst of all, she CALMS DOWN. No longer is she the fiesty warrior princess I grew to love, but some gentle, mild-mannered FAIRY. Ugh! <br />(P.S. This shelf is actually supposed to be called action-adventure-the-occasional-pirate, but the stupid computer kind of forgot the "ate" part at the end of "pirate". Just in case you were wondering. </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1269222344">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16122686877508889270">This was a very fun and fantastic book! <br /><br />Princess Addie and her sister Meryl live in the kingdom of Bamarre. Meryl is strong, bold and brave while Addie is even scared at the sight of a spider. However, when Meryl catches the grey death, a sickness with no cure, Addie must set off on an exciting adventure across the land. <br /><br />I would recommend this book to anyone who enjoys adventure, fantasy, and just the right amount of romance!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a href="/review/list/39049180-megan-severance?shelf=favorites" class="actionLinkLite">favorites</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1334955181">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8511927569498376851">Perhaps because I can never resist a fairy story, or perhaps because I fell in love with <em>Ella Enchanted</em> and was starving for more, or perhaps because what drew me was the love - pure, unconditional, secure - between Meryl and Addie (so much like my sister and I), I believe I can say with truth that this book is one of the best I've ever read. Artfully written, <em>The Two Princesses of Bamarre</em> has everything I adore in a good tale: adventure, a journey, magical races, romance... in short, Gail Carso</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8511927569498376851">Perhaps because I can never resist a fairy story, or perhaps because I fell in love with <em>Ella Enchanted</em> and was starving for more, or perhaps because what drew me was the love - pure, unconditional, secure - between Meryl and Addie (so much like my sister and I), I believe I can say with truth that this book is one of the best I've ever read. Artfully written, <em>The Two Princesses of Bamarre</em> has everything I adore in a good tale: adventure, a journey, magical races, romance... in short, Gail Carson Levine has done it again with this beautiful story. Through the pages, the goal remains clear - find the cure for the Grey Death, and save Meryl - and this is my favorite part. Addie, the heroine, is determined to stop Death from stealing her sister. It is <em>love</em> that keeps her going, not courage - but courage she finds, and honor, and the knowledge that though things may change, Meryl will always be there for her.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1212315887">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1212315887" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/13228718-paperdollmom" class="left imgcol" title="paperdollmom"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1389479759p2/13228718.jpg" alt="paperdollmom" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1212315887?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 26, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/13228718-paperdollmom" class="user" title="paperdollmom">paperdollmom</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a onclick="Effect.toggle('reviewTextContainer1212315887'); return false;" href="#">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span style="display:none" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1212315887">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3645739538872495535">I cannot believe I read through this book so quickly! It was a fast, fluffy read, one that I am glad I accomplished. However, I am conflicted over this book, and unsure how many stars I would give it. The plot is wonderful, revolving around sisterly love and bravery and courage. It sounds like a book that would be perfect for my liking, which is why I purchased it. I could go into depth about what displeased me, but I don't really think it is necessary. I think that basically this author's writi</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3645739538872495535">I cannot believe I read through this book so quickly! It was a fast, fluffy read, one that I am glad I accomplished. However, I am conflicted over this book, and unsure how many stars I would give it. The plot is wonderful, revolving around sisterly love and bravery and courage. It sounds like a book that would be perfect for my liking, which is why I purchased it. I could go into depth about what displeased me, but I don't really think it is necessary. I think that basically this author's writing style comes across a bit too young for me in most places and some specific details in the book have me slightly wincing at the silliness. Don't get me wrong, this is a fabulous fairytale type of book, however, I have read much better that I found myself, in a way, comparing it to while reading. Even though I have not read a tale even close to this storyline (which I do admire), the finished piece was not put together well enough for my taste. I think I just have really high standards for fairytales, expecting perfection and to be absolutely wowed, simply because fairytales in general leave me in awe. I was not left in awe, but admired the author's creative plot and effort. <br /><br />The thing I did really did like about this book was the creative take on sorcerers and dragons. I loved Rhys and all his quirks and how a dragon's laughter sounded like bells. It was refreshing to read the scenes that talked of Rhys or dragons. What I didn't like was when the author tried to pass minor events as a major one, or have a character come to a thought or an idea that seemed out of character, or too all of a sudden. I was also a little put off with the ending. The ending was wonderful, but I didn't like how she wrote the reactions of the characters in the ending chapters. I just didn't get why she was trying to force a happy ending into a bittersweet ending. It was weird for me.<br /><br />Overall, I am glad I read it. I've been meaning to give a Gail Carson Levine novel a try for a long time. I don't know if this novel is a good representation of the general style of her novels overall, but I don't see myself picking up anymore of her books. I see myself reaching more for fairytales written by Mercedes Lackey or Dennis L. McKiernan.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3645739538872495535">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_132868450">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/132868450" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4579690-small-review" class="left imgcol" title="Small Review"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1291348460p2/4579690.jpg" alt="Small Review" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/132868450?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 11, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4579690-small-review" class="user" title="Small Review">Small Review</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/4579690-small-review?shelf=library-own" class="actionLinkLite">library-own</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4579690-small-review?shelf=g-fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">g-fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4579690-small-review?shelf=read-2010" class="actionLinkLite">read-2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer132868450">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13622346284266264678">I've heard nothing but fantastic things about Gail Carson Levine, but for some reason I had it in my head that she wrote "simple" stories. Maybe they were good, but I just wasn’t expecting all that much from them. My only exposure had been watching the movie Ella Enchanted (cute, but nothing amazing) and one of her fairy short stories (again, cute, but forgettable). Granted, not a fair account, but that’s where I was. I had picked up this copy at a garage sale and finally decided to read it (ful</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13622346284266264678">I've heard nothing but fantastic things about Gail Carson Levine, but for some reason I had it in my head that she wrote "simple" stories. Maybe they were good, but I just wasn’t expecting all that much from them. My only exposure had been watching the movie Ella Enchanted (cute, but nothing amazing) and one of her fairy short stories (again, cute, but forgettable). Granted, not a fair account, but that’s where I was. I had picked up this copy at a garage sale and finally decided to read it (fully expecting to give it away when I was finished). Let me just say, I was so wrong about Gail Carson Levine!<br /><br />Addie was such a good character. She was meek and the exact type of person the phrase “Scared of her own shadow” would apply to. She always lived in the shadow of her bold sister, and she was perfectly happy to stay there. I, like Addie, was always content to stay in the background while my friends took center stage. Because of this, I felt an instant connection with Addie.<br /><br />While much of the plot was predictable and neatly tied together, the story didn't feel stale or boring at all. It is obvious from the outset that Addie will find courage, but her progression from timid coward to capable woman is paced well and enjoyable to read. I appreciated that Levine had Addie find courage in her own way. She never became a daring swordswoman charging into battle like her sister, but she instead found confidence in her own strengths and abilities. This made for a nice “Stay true to yourself” message without being overly preachy.<br /><br />The quality of world building in this story surprised me, in a good way. The specters added a level of fear and interest that was different from the norm. They could appear as anyone, and so they often tried to trick the characters by pretending to be benign people. This concept was creepy, and the puzzle that presented in having to figure out who was real and who was a specter made for some fun scenes.<br /><br />Often dragons are written pretty similar to human characters with very human-like personalities. This dragon wasn't very human at all. Though she possessed some human-like traits, overall her way of thinking was definitely different. She wasn't a villain, but she wasn't good either. She was a complex character older tweens and teens will probably appreciate.<br /><br />The objects Addie has with her on her journey allowed for even more inventive scenes. Reading about and trying to guess how she should best use these resources was fun. The epic poem about the hero Drualt woven throughout the story also added a layer of depth to the world and was a nice way for the author to foreshadow events.<br /><br />The ending was not my ideal, but it worked. I wasn't expecting to like this story as much as I did, but it was a fun, nice read and I was pleasantly surprised. This should be a hit among tween girls, and would make for a great recommendation to girls who are a little shy or insecure. While not a tween, I still enjoyed this story very much. <br /><br />4.5 stars</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13622346284266264678">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <a href="/user/show/5576010-carol-hardesty" class="user" title="Carol Hardesty">Carol Hardesty</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,

              <span style="display:none" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer175105165">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4355439182770338384">Following the success of her award-winning debut "Ella Enchanted", Gail Carson Levine decided to try her hand at writing an original fairytale. As you can tell by the one-star rating, I was bitterly disappointed by it. True, Ms. Levine's prose is as elegant here as it was in "Ella", but that was the only positive thing about "The Two Princesses of Bamarre". I was originally drawn to the story because the title characters sounded a lot like my older sister and me. Lynn (my sister) is definitely M</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4355439182770338384">Following the success of her award-winning debut "Ella Enchanted", Gail Carson Levine decided to try her hand at writing an original fairytale. As you can tell by the one-star rating, I was bitterly disappointed by it. True, Ms. Levine's prose is as elegant here as it was in "Ella", but that was the only positive thing about "The Two Princesses of Bamarre". I was originally drawn to the story because the title characters sounded a lot like my older sister and me. Lynn (my sister) is definitely Meryl; mature and brave. And I'm totally Addie; immature and shy. But when I actually read the book, I couldn't believe how bad it turned out to be. Most of the characters are uninteresting. There's too much fantasy and not enough realism to make it a conceivable make-believe world. (That made sense, right?) Worst of all, Addie fails in her quest to save Meryl. Part of the reason we love fairytales so much is because the heroes are able to overcome the impossible odds to get their happy endings. I thought Ms. Levine knew that, but I guess I was wrong. </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/492580043?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 02, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/15968317-caylee" class="user" title="Caylee">Caylee</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/15968317-caylee?shelf=favorites" class="actionLinkLite">favorites</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer492580043">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14630067603256693257">I was given "The Two Princesses of Bamarre" as a birthday present and at first I was skeptical about reading it but when I finally sat down and opened it, I was hugely impressed. I loved that book and I have read it five times so far. It appealed to me because I like fantasy and I am a feminist, so I was mentally cheering Addie on when she left for her quest to find the cure for the Gray Death.<br />I have always been a lot like Addie, artistic and clever but shy and worrying. So when she started to b</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14630067603256693257">I was given "The Two Princesses of Bamarre" as a birthday present and at first I was skeptical about reading it but when I finally sat down and opened it, I was hugely impressed. I loved that book and I have read it five times so far. It appealed to me because I like fantasy and I am a feminist, so I was mentally cheering Addie on when she left for her quest to find the cure for the Gray Death.<br />I have always been a lot like Addie, artistic and clever but shy and worrying. So when she started to become braver I was happy for her. <br />I liked the dragon Vollys, I understood she was lonely but I did not feel sympathetic for her in the end.<br />The choice Meryl make near the end of the book (I won't say what it is because it would spoil the book, but those who have read it will know what I am talking about) is not the choice I would make as much as I would love the adventures I wouldn't want to live forever.<br />I enjoyed the book and I think, if you enjoy fantasy you should try it. It is not just a silly fairytale about princesses.<br />I have given the book 5 stars and I think it deserves every one of them.</span>

  <a href="/user/show/10123015-grace" class="left imgcol" title="Grace"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" alt="Grace" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/345843985?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 10, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/10123015-grace" class="user" title="Grace">Grace</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a onclick="Effect.toggle('reviewTextContainer345843985'); return false;" href="#">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span style="display:none" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer345843985">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9743341276938594180">I just finished reading this book for the second time. The first time I read it was when I was in third grade and I loved it then, so I wanted to re-read it and see if I still loved it or not. When I first started this book for the second time, it was kind of boring and I thought it was an easy read. But as I continued to read it, I was drawn into the story and I felt like I was traveling with Princess Addie (the main character) throughout her journey. I was there with her as she fought gryphons</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9743341276938594180">I just finished reading this book for the second time. The first time I read it was when I was in third grade and I loved it then, so I wanted to re-read it and see if I still loved it or not. When I first started this book for the second time, it was kind of boring and I thought it was an easy read. But as I continued to read it, I was drawn into the story and I felt like I was traveling with Princess Addie (the main character) throughout her journey. I was there with her as she fought gryphons, spectors and ogres, as she searched for a cure to save her sister from the Grey Death, and as she found romance. I think the first time I read it I didn't truly understand everything that was going on and I didn't notice some stuff, but after re-reading this book I was refreshed and I fell in love with it for the second time. I had a new understanding and appreciation for the book. Although I loved it, there were some things I was disappointed about. I was upset that Meryl, Addie's sister, becomes a fairy at the end instead of returning to her life at the palace with Addie. I was also mad that Gavin, a boy from a village, died while helping Addie and Meryl reach the cure. He was one of my favorite characters for his bravery and willingness to help the two princesses. I did like it though when Addie met the famous Drualt and how he was helping her the whole time throughout her enitre journey. Despite my dislikes though, The Two Princesses of Bamarre is definitley one of my favorite books written by Gail Carson Levine, along with Ella Enchanted. I really like Levine's writting style and how she incorperates adventure, romance and fantasy all into one book. In my opinion, this was without a doubt one of the best books she's ever written. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9743341276938594180">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/13677.Gail_Carson_Levine">About Gail Carson Levine</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/13677.Gail_Carson_Levine"><img alt="13677" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1432495575p2/13677.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer16600915032017242563">Just letting you all know: I'm only going to review books I love. There's enough negative criticism without me piling on. A book is too hard to write.<br /><br />Gail Carson Levine grew up in New York City and began writing seriously in 1987. Her first book for children, Ella Enchanted, was a 1998 Newbery Honor Book. Levine's other books include Fairest; Dave at Night, an ALA Notable Book and Best Book for Yo</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16600915032017242563">Just letting you all know: I'm only going to review books I love. There's enough negative criticism without me piling on. A book is too hard to write.<br /><br />Gail Carson Levine grew up in New York City and began writing seriously in 1987. Her first book for children, Ella Enchanted, was a 1998 Newbery Honor Book. Levine's other books include Fairest; Dave at Night, an ALA Notable Book and Best Book for Young Adults; The Wish; The Two Princesses of Bamarre; and the six Princess Tales books. She is also the author of the nonfiction book Writing Magic: Creating Stories That Fly and the picture book Betsy Who Cried Wolf, illustrated by Scott Nash. Gail, her husband, David, and their Airedale, Baxter, live in a 1790 farmhouse in the Hudson River Valley of New York State.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16600915032017242563">...more</a>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/3155307-the-two-princesses-of-bamarre">Quotes from The Two Princesse...</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div tyle="padding-bottom:15px" class="stacked">
            <span class="readable">“Step follows step,<br />Hope follows Courage,<br />Set your face towards danger,<br />Set your heart on victory.”</span>
            <nobr>
              —
              <a href="/quotes/34447-step-follows-step-hope-follows-courage-set-your-face-towards" class="actionLinkLite">518 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div tyle="padding-bottom:15px" class="stacked">
            <span class="readable">“Drualt took Freya's warm hand,<br />Her strong hand,<br />Her sword hand,<br />And pressed it to his lips,<br />Pressed it to his heart.<br />Come with me,' he said.<br />Come with me to battle,<br />My love. Tarry at my side.<br />Stay with me<br />When battle is done.<br />Tarry at my side.<br />Laugh with me,<br />And walk with me<br />The long, long way.<br />Tarry with me,<br />My love, at my side.”</span>
            <nobr>
              —
              <a href="/quotes/45709-drualt-took-freya-s-warm-hand-her-strong-hand-her-sword" class="actionLinkLite">139 likes</a>
